Iteration 1: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and the value indicates a binary (0 or 1) indicator. The goal is to analyze the evidence and assess whether the claim is logically and factually supported by the data.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the Evidence**: Each key-value pair represents a piece of information. The value (0 or 1) indicates whether the entity or concept is associated with the claim in the evidence.
2. **Identify the Claim**: The claim is a specific assertion about a person, event, or concept.
3. **Check for Direct Support**: If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., the claim states that John Cutler conducted the Terre Haute experiments, and the evidence shows he did), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
4. **Check for Direct Contradiction**: If the evidence contradicts the claim (e.g., the claim states John Cutler conducted the experiments, but the evidence shows he did not), then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
5. **Consider Context and Common Knowledge**: If the claim is about a well-known historical event or figure, use common knowledge to assess whether the evidence supports it. If the evidence is insufficient or conflicting, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence:
- **Claim**: "John Charles Cutler conducted the Terre Haute prison experiments and was involved in observing the natural progression of untreated syphilis in rural American-American men in Alabama."
- **Evidence**: 
  - `{'key': 'John Charles Cutler', 'value': 0}`
  - `{'key': 'Tuskegee syphilis experiment', 'value': 0}`
  - `{'key': 'Tuskegee syphilis experiment', 'value': 1}`
  - `{'key': 'Terre Haute prison experiments', 'value': 0}`

- **Reasoning**: The evidence shows that John Charles Cutler has a value of 0 for both the Terre Haute prison experiments and the Tuskegee syphilis experiment, indicating he was not involved in either. The Tuskegee experiment is well-documented as being conducted by the U.S. Public Health Service, not by John Cutler. Thus, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Important Notes:
- The evidence may not be exhaustive, but it is the only data available.
- If the evidence is ambiguous or conflicting, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim is about a well-known event or figure, use common knowledge to assess its validity, but the evidence must be the primary basis for the determination.

### Final Answer:
Provide a verdict of **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, and a brief reasoning explaining how the evidence supports or contradicts the claim.

Iteration 2: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a collection of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., a location, person, event, or product), and each value is a numerical code or indicator (e.g., 0 or 1).  

### Task Description  
- **Key-Value Pairs**: Each entry in the evidence is a pair of a **key** (e.g., "North Blenheim, New York", "Hurricane Irene") and a **value** (e.g., 0 or 2).  
- **Claim**: A statement that asserts a specific relationship between an entity and an event, outcome, or characteristic.  
- **Evidence Analysis**:  
  - The key-value pairs may represent data about the entity (e.g., damage, ownership, influence, etc.).  
  - The value may indicate a presence, absence, or degree of impact (e.g., 0 = no impact, 1 = impact, 2 = significant impact).  
  - The values are not necessarily descriptive in nature, but may be used to infer relationships or outcomes.  

### Reasoning Steps  
1. **Identify the entity and claim**: Determine the specific entity (e.g., "North Blenheim, New York") and the claim (e.g., "was destroyed by flooding caused by Hurricane Irene").  
2. **Analyze the evidence**: Check if the evidence supports the claim by linking the entity to the claim using the key-value pairs.  
3. **Check for contradictions or missing information**:  
   - Is there any evidence that directly supports the claim?  
   - Are there any contradictions or gaps in the evidence that weaken the claim?  
   - Are the values meaningful in the context of the claim?  
4. **Determine the verdict**:  
   - If the evidence directly supports the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
   - If the evidence contradicts the claim or lacks sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Entity types**: The keys may refer to locations, people, events, products, or other entities.  
- **Value interpretation**: The values may represent data such as damage, ownership, influence, or presence.  
- **Geographical or temporal context**: Some keys may be specific to locations or events in a particular time frame.  
- **Cultural or contextual relevance**: Some claims may require knowledge of cultural, historical, or industry-specific contexts.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., a key-value pair links the entity to the claim and the value indicates a positive or relevant outcome), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
- If the evidence contradicts the claim or lacks necessary information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Example:  
**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'North Blenheim, New York', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'Hurricane Irene', 'value': 0}  

**Claim**: "North Blenheim, New York was destroyed by flooding caused by the Hurricane that landed in August 2011."  

**Reasoning**:  
- The value 2 for "North Blenheim, New York" may indicate a high level of damage, but the evidence does not provide any direct information about the impact of Hurricane Irene.  
- The value 0 for "Hurricane Irene" may indicate no impact, but this does not confirm or deny the claim.  
- The evidence is insufficient to determine the relationship between the entity and the claim.  

**Conclusion**: The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

Iteration 3: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., person, place, or thing) and each value represents a numerical or categorical attribute. 

### Key Details to Consider:
- The **evidence** may include:
  - Names of people, places, or organizations.
  - Numerical values (e.g., 0, 2, 100) that could represent counts, rankings, or other attributes.
  - Relationships or associations between entities (e.g., "X is associated with Y", "Z is not associated with W").

- The **claim** is a statement about a specific person, event, or relationship that must be evaluated based on the evidence.

### Task Description:
- **Step 1:** Analyze the evidence to understand what it tells us about the entities mentioned.
- **Step 2:** Determine if the claim can be logically inferred from the evidence.
- **Step 3:** If the claim is fully supported by the evidence, mark it as **SUPPORTED**.
- **Step 4:** If the claim cannot be confirmed or contradicted by the evidence, mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- If the evidence contains **no direct or indirect information** about the claim, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence **directly supports** the claim, it is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence **contradicts** the claim, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
**Evidence:**  
{'key': 'Buzz Arlett', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'Mike Hessman', 'value': 0}  

**Claim:**  
"The man who broke Buzz Arlett's home run record played first baseman and third baseman."

**Output:**  
**NOT_SUPPORTED** (as in Example 1)

### Notes:
- The assistant should avoid making assumptions beyond the provided evidence.
- The assistant should not rely on external knowledge or common knowledge unless explicitly stated in the evidence.
- The assistant should treat all entities and values as given and not interpret them in a way that is not explicitly stated.

### Final Answer:
- **SUPPORTED** if the claim is fully and directly supported by the evidence.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the claim is not supported by the evidence, contradicted, or if the evidence is insufficient to determine the claim.

### Task Description

- **Claim**: A statement that makes a specific assertion about a person, event, or entity.  
- **Evidence Analysis**:  
  - The evidence may include information about the entity's nationality, profession, location, or other attributes.  
  - The claim may include specific details like birth years, educational background, or professional roles.  
  - The claim may involve assertions about the entity's activities, such as teaching, composing, or translating.

2. **Match with Evidence**: Check if the evidence supports the claim by matching attributes (e.g., nationality, profession, location, birth year, etc.).  
3. **Check for Missing Information**: Determine if any critical details of the claim are not mentioned in the evidence.  
4. **Evaluate Consistency**: Ensure that the claim aligns with the evidence in terms of accuracy and logical consistency.  
5. **Determine Support or Not Support**: Based on the above, decide whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider  
- **Names and Titles**: Ensure that the key names (e.g., "Vincent Kling (translator)", "Hugo von Hofmannsthal") are correctly matched with the values.  
- **Geographic and Temporal Context**: If the claim involves a location (e.g., "University of Vienna") or a time period (e.g., "1874"), ensure that the evidence includes relevant information.  
- **Professional Roles**: If the claim involves a profession (e.g., "translator", "composer", "teacher"), ensure that the evidence includes relevant attributes.  
- **Cultural and Historical Context**: If the claim involves a composer, artist, or writer from a specific culture or era, ensure that the evidence includes relevant historical or cultural information.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- Use the key-value pairs to infer attributes of the entity mentioned in the claim.  
- If the claim includes specific details (e.g., birth year, profession, location) that are not present in the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the claim is consistent with the evidence and includes all necessary details, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Example Output Format  
**Answer**: **SUPPORTED** / **NOT_SUPPORTED**  
**Reasoning**: [Step-by-step reasoning based on the evidence and claim]

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the **evidence** provided. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., author, film title, book title, event, etc.), and each value represents a numerical or categorical indicator (e.g., 0 or 1, or a category like "production company", "director", "genre", etc.).

### Task Description:

1. **Analyze the Evidence**:  
   - Each key in the evidence represents a specific entity or attribute.  
   - Each value represents a numerical or categorical indicator that may be used to infer relationships or associations between the key and the claim.

2. **Interpret the Evidence**:  
   - Identify which keys are associated with the claim (e.g., "Walt Disney Pictures", "Donovan Cook", "McFarland, USA", etc.).  
   - Determine whether the value associated with the key provides evidence that supports or contradicts the claim.

3. **Evaluate the Claim**:  
   - If the evidence directly or indirectly supports the claim (e.g., a key-value pair indicates that a company produced a film, or a person directed a film), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
   - If the evidence does not provide sufficient information to support the claim, or if it contradicts the claim, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

4. **Consider the Context**:  
   - Be cautious about interpreting the values as literal or categorical indicators.  
   - If the value is not clearly defined, it may be difficult to determine its meaning.  
   - If the claim involves a specific entity (e.g., a film, book, company), ensure that the evidence directly or indirectly references that entity.

### Example:

#### Inputs:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'McFarland, USA', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Donovan Cook', 'value': 0}  

Claim: Walt Disney Pictures helped produce both the film directed by Donovan Cook and McFarland, USA.

#### Output:
**Answer: NOT_SUPPORTED**

### Important Notes:
- The values (0 or 1) are not always clear, but they are used to indicate a relationship or association.  
- The claim must be directly supported by the evidence, not inferred or assumed.  
- If the evidence does not mention the claim's subject (e.g., the company, person, or film), then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer:
Please provide the **claim** and the **evidence** in the specified format, and I will determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

Iteration 6: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a song, a person, a fact, or a reference), and the value indicates a binary or qualitative association (e.g., 0 or 1, or a presence/absence of a relationship).

### Task Description

- **Input Format**: The evidence is a dictionary of key-value pairs, where:
  - **Key**: A specific identifier (e.g., "Bebe Rexha", "Hey Mama (David Guetta song)", "I Don't Wanna Grow Up").
  - **Value**: A number (0 or 1) or a qualitative indicator (e.g., "associated", "not associated", "present", "absent").

- **Claim**: A statement that makes a specific assertion about a relationship between entities (e.g., "A song by David Guetta was produced by the Dutch DJ Afrojack. The signer who recorded 'I Don't Wanna Grow Up' guested on this song.").

- **Task**: Analyze the claim by evaluating whether the evidence supports the assertion. If the evidence directly or indirectly confirms the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**. If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Key Considerations

- **Binary Values**: Use the value (0 or 1) to determine if a relationship exists or not.
- **Qualitative Indicators**: If the value is not 0 or 1, interpret it as a qualitative indicator (e.g., "associated", "not associated").
- **Entity Relationships**: Determine if the claim involves relationships between entities (e.g., song producer, guest artist, etc.).
- **Logical Consistency**: Ensure that the claim and the evidence are logically consistent. If the claim requires information not present in the evidence, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example

#### Inputs
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Bebe Rexha', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Hey Mama (David Guetta song)', 'value': 0}  
{'key': "I Don't Wanna Grow Up", 'value': 0}  

Claim:  
"A song by David Guetta was produced by the Dutch DJ Afrojack. The signer who recorded 'I Don't Wanna Grow Up' guested on this song."

#### Output
**NOT_SUPPORTED** (as in Example 1)

### Generalizable Strategy

1. **Identify the claim** and break it into individual assertions.
2. **Check each assertion** against the evidence.
3. **Use the value** to determine if the relationship exists or not.
4. **Evaluate the logical consistency** of the claim with the evidence.
5. **Conclude whether the claim is supported or not** based on the analysis.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts

- **Music Industry**: Understanding song producers, artists, and their relationships is critical for evaluating claims about music production and guest appearances.
- **Historical and Cultural Context**: For claims involving historical figures or cultural references, context is essential to determine accuracy.
- **Data Interpretation**: Values (0 or 1) must be interpreted carefully, as they may represent presence, absence, or other qualitative indicators.

This approach ensures that the assistant can reason through complex claims involving multiple entities and relationships, using the provided evidence effectively.

Iteration 7: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a person's name, a location, a historical event, or a product), and each value is either `0` or `1`, indicating whether the key is present or absent in the evidence.

### **Task Description:**

1. **Understand the Claim**: The claim is a statement that asserts a relationship between two entities (e.g., a person, a location, or an event) based on their attributes.

2. **Analyze the Evidence**: The evidence consists of a list of key-value pairs. Each key represents a fact or piece of information, and the value indicates whether that fact is present (1) or absent (0) in the evidence.

3. **Identify Relevant Entities**: Extract the relevant entities mentioned in the claim and compare them with the evidence.

4. **Compare Attributes**: For each entity in the claim, compare their attributes (e.g., country, profession, event, etc.) with the evidence to determine if the claim is supported.

5. **Determine Support or Not Support**: Based on the evidence, determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** (the evidence directly supports the claim) or **NOT_SUPPORTED** (the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information).

### **Important Notes:**

- The values (`0` or `1`) in the evidence are not numerical values but rather **indicators** of presence or absence of a specific fact.
- If a key is not present in the evidence, it is considered **not provided** or **not relevant** to the claim.
- If a key is present (value = 1), it is considered **provided** and may be used to support or contradict the claim.
- The **claim** may involve comparisons between two or more entities (e.g., "A is from a country closer to X than B").

### **Example:**

**Claim**: "The tennis player Kenneth or Ken Eliot Flach is from a country closer to Ontario, Canada than the woman who defeated Maria Sharapova in the 2015 French Open – Women's Singles."

**Evidence**:  
- {'key': 'Ken Flach', 'value': 0}  
- {'key': 'Lucie Šafářová', 'value': 0}  
- {'key': "2015 French Open – Women's Singles", 'value': 0}

**Reasoning**:  
- Ken Flach is from Australia (value = 0, not provided).  
- Lucie Šafářová is from the Czech Republic (value = 0, not provided).  
- The claim compares the country of Ken Flach to the country of the woman who defeated Maria Sharapova (Lucie Šafářová).  
- The evidence does not provide the country of either individual, so the claim cannot be evaluated based on the given evidence.

### **Output Format:**

- **SUPPORTED**: If the evidence directly supports the claim.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information.

### **Generalizable Strategy:**

- Use the evidence to identify the relevant entities and their attributes.
- Compare the attributes of the claim's entities with the evidence.
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, the verdict is **SUPPORTED**; otherwise, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

---

### **Niche and Domain-Specific Information:**

- The evidence may include **taxonomic information**, **historical events**, **personnel details**, **geographical locations**, or **product data**.
- The values (`0` or `1`) may represent **presence/absence** in a dataset or **classification** (e.g., whether a species is in a particular group).
- The claim may involve **comparative statements** (e.g., "A is closer to X than B").
- The assistant must be able to interpret the meaning of the key-value pairs and their relationship to the claim.

---

### **Final Output:**

- **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the analysis of the evidence and the claim.

### Task Description:

- **Evidence**: A collection of key-value pairs that may or may not support the claim.

2. Match the claim's subject to the evidence keys.
3. Check if the value associated with the key supports the claim.
4. Evaluate whether the claim is logically supported by the evidence.
5. If the evidence is insufficient or contradictory, mark the claim as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information.

- The assistant should avoid making assumptions beyond the provided evidence.

### **Example Guidelines:**  
- If the claim is about a person and the evidence shows they are not mentioned (value 0), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the claim is about a specific event and the evidence shows that the event is associated with a value of `1` or `2`, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

- The claim may involve **genres** (e.g., "romantic comedy") or **cast members** (e.g., "Michael Shannon", "Kirsten Dunst").  
- The **numeric values** in the evidence are used to infer **relevance**, **presence**, or **absence** of the claim's elements.  

### **Generalizable Strategy:**  
- **Compare the claim** to the evidence and assess whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts the claim.  
- **Use the numeric values** as a proxy for the strength of the evidence.  
- **Consider the context** of the claim (e.g., time, genre, person) when evaluating the evidence.

```
### Task Description:

- **Key-Value Pairs**: Each entry in the evidence is a key-value pair. The key represents a concept (e.g., "Cyathodes", "Gymnocalycium eurypleurum", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and the value is a numerical score (0 or 1). A value of 0 typically indicates no information, while a value of 1 indicates that information is present or confirmed.
  
- **Claim**: A statement that asserts a fact or relationship between entities (e.g., "Cyathodes is a type of plant", "The species that may grow in association with Gymnocalycium eurypleurum is also a type of plant").

- **Reasoning Process**:
  - Analyze the evidence to determine if it provides any direct or indirect support for the claim.
  - If the claim is about a classification (e.g., "Cyathodes is a type of plant"), check if the evidence includes any information about the classification of the entity.
  - If the claim is about an association (e.g., "The species that may grow in association with Gymnocalycium eurypleurum is also a type of plant"), check if the evidence includes any information about species associated with the given entity.

- **Output**:
  - If the evidence supports the claim, the verdict is **SUPPORTED**.
  - If the evidence does not support the claim and is inconsistent with it, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:

**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'Cyathodes', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Gymnocalycium eurypleurum', 'value': 1}  

**Claim**:  
"Cyathodes is a type of plant. The species that may grow in association with Gymnocalycium eurypleurum is also a type of plant."

**Output**:  
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

### Notes:
- The evidence does not provide any information about the classification of "Cyathodes" or any species associated with "Gymnocalycium eurypleurum".
- The value of 0 in the evidence indicates the absence of information, not a confirmation or denial of the claim.
- If the claim is about a well-known entity (e.g., "The Sandman" by Neil Gaiman), the evidence may not include direct information, but the claim may still be **SUPPORTED** if the evidence indirectly supports it (e.g., through general knowledge).

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the value of the key to determine if the evidence supports or contradicts the claim.
- If the key is not present in the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the key is present and the value is 1, the evidence supports the claim.
- If the key is present and the value is 0, the evidence does not support the claim.
- If the claim is about a classification, the evidence must include information about the classification.
- If the claim is about an association, the evidence must include information about species associated with the given entity.
```

Iteration 15: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., historical events, people, organizations, or films), and each value represents a count or a boolean indicator (e.g., 1 for "true", 0 for "false").

### Task Overview

- **Task:** Analyze the provided evidence and determine if the given **claim** is **factually accurate** or **not**.
- **Evidence Format:** A dictionary of key-value pairs, where each key is a string representing a fact or event, and each value is an integer (0 or 1) indicating whether that fact is present (1) or not (0).
- **Claim Format:** A statement that asserts a specific fact or relationship between entities.

### Reasoning Guidelines

1. **Identify the claim:** Clearly understand what the claim is asserting.
2. **Match the claim to the evidence:** Check if the claim is supported by any of the evidence (i.e., if the evidence contains facts that directly support the claim).
3. **Check for contradictions or missing information:** Ensure that the claim is not contradicted by the evidence, and that all parts of the claim are addressed.
4. **Determine the verdict:** If the claim is fully supported by the evidence, the verdict is **SUPPORTED**. If the claim is not supported or contradicted by the evidence, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example

#### Inputs:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Confederate States presidential election, 1861', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Jefferson Davis', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'White House of the Confederacy', 'value': 1}  

Claim:  
"The sole President of the White House of the Confederacy was the United States Secretary of War. This Secretary of War under Franklin Pierce was elected President under the Provisional Confederate States Constitution."

#### Output:

```  
### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the evidence**: The values may indicate:
   - A presence or absence of a specific attribute (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent).
   - A numerical ranking or category (e.g., 2 = plant, 0 = not a plant).
   - A placeholder or missing data (e.g., 0 = unknown or not recorded).

2. **Analyze the claim**: The claim is a statement about the relationship between two or more entities (e.g., "Arthur Hiller Penn was born before George Kuchar").

3. **Use logical reasoning**:
   - If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., "George Kuchar was born in 1945" and "Arthur Penn was born in 1940"), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
   - If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

4. **Be careful with ambiguous or incomplete data**:
   - If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous (e.g., "value: 0" without context), it should not be used to support or refute the claim.
   - If the evidence does not provide any relevant information about the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

5. **Use only the given evidence and no external knowledge**:
   - Do not assume any external knowledge or context beyond the provided evidence.
   - Only use the provided evidence to make a judgment.
  ```  

  ```  
     - **Value** is a numerical value (e.g., 2, 0, 1, or other numbers) that represents some metric or count related to that category.

2. **Interpret the Values:**
   - The values are interpreted based on the context of the key. For example:
     - A value of `2` might indicate that a band has released 2 rock albums.
     - A value of `0` might indicate that a band has not released any rock albums.
     - A value of `1` might indicate that a song is associated with a particular event or category.

3. **Evaluate the Claim:**
   - The claim is a statement about a specific relationship between entities (e.g., "The band that released the album The General Electric has released more rock albums than Morningwood").
   - You must analyze the evidence to determine if the claim is **supported** or **not supported** based on the data provided.

4. **Reason Step-by-Step:**
   - Identify which entities are mentioned in the claim.
   - Match those entities to the evidence.
   - Compare the values to determine if the claim is logically consistent with the evidence.
   - If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
   - If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

5. **Final Answer:**
   - Provide a clear and concise verdict: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
   - Include a brief reasoning step-by-step to justify your conclusion.

- {'key': 'Shihad', 'value': 2}
- {'key': 'Morningwood', 'value': 2}
- {'key': 'The General Electric', 'value': 0}

"The band that released the album The General Electric has released more rock albums than Morningwood."

**Reasoning:**
- The band **The General Electric** has a value of `0` (0 rock albums).
- The band **Morningwood** has a value of `2` (2 rock albums).
- Therefore, **Morningwood** has released more rock albums than **The General Electric**.

**Final Answer: NOT_SUPPORTED**

### Key Notes:
- The values may represent counts, associations, or other metrics, and the interpretation depends on context.
- The assistant must be careful to avoid making assumptions about the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
```  

Iteration 25: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a player's name, a team's name, a scientific genus, a song title, etc.), and each value represents a numerical or categorical value associated with that key.

### Task Description

- **Step-by-step Analysis**:  
  - For each key in the evidence, interpret the value and understand what it represents.  
  - Cross-reference the evidence with the claim to determine if the claim is logically supported by the evidence.  
  - Identify any contradictions or missing information that could weaken the claim.  

- **Key Considerations**:  
  - If the claim is about a **specific person, team, event, or object** (e.g., a musician, a song, a player, a scientific genus), then the evidence must directly or indirectly support that claim.  
  - If the claim is about a **general fact** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii has more species than Lantana"), then the evidence must provide numerical or categorical support for that general statement.  
  - If the claim is about **historical or chronological information** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii was introduced to Hawaii in 1902"), then the evidence must include that specific information or a direct reference to it.  
  - If the claim is about **causality, association, or timing** (e.g., "Silibinin was discovered in 1925"), then the evidence must include that specific time or discovery information.  

- **Final Decision**:  
  - If the claim is **fully supported** by the evidence (i.e., all parts of the claim are directly or indirectly confirmed by the evidence), then the verdict is **SUPPORTED**.  
  - If the claim is **not fully supported** by the evidence (i.e., there is missing information, contradiction, or insufficient evidence), then the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Example Format

Iteration 26: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the **provided evidence**. The evidence consists of a dictionary where each key represents a piece of information (e.g., a person, a band, an event, or a fact), and each value represents a numerical or categorical indicator (e.g., 0, 1, 2, or a category like "pop", "rock", "classical", etc.).

### Task Description:
- **Step 1:** Analyze the **evidence** to extract relevant information about the **claim's subject** (e.g., the person, band, event, or fact being discussed).
- **Step 2:** Determine if the **claim** can be logically supported by the **evidence**. This includes checking for:
  - Direct or indirect evidence of the claim's truth.
  - Logical consistency between the claim and the evidence.
  - The absence of contradictory or conflicting information.
- **Step 3:** Based on the analysis, decide whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** (if the evidence directly or indirectly supports the claim) or **NOT_SUPPORTED** (if the evidence does not support the claim or contradicts it).

### Key Considerations:
- The **value** in the evidence dictionary may indicate a rating, classification, or identifier (e.g., 0 for "not applicable", 1 for "yes", or a category like "pop", "rock", "classical", etc.).
- The **key** in the evidence dictionary represents the subject of the claim (e.g., "Ray Wilson", "Billy Idol", "Capital Cities (band)", "Spencer Ludwig", "Herbert Matthews", "Fulgencio Batista", etc.).
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** about the **claim's subject**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence directly supports** the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence contradicts** the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Ray Wilson (musician)', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Billy Idol', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Live and Acoustic (Ray Wilson album)', 'value': 0}  

Claim: The musician that released the rock CD "Live and Acoustic" is younger than Billy Idol.  

**Reasoning:**  
- The evidence shows that **Ray Wilson** is associated with the album **"Live and Acoustic"**, but it does not provide any information about their **age**.  
- The claim assumes a specific age relationship between **Ray Wilson** and **Billy Idol**, which is not supported by the evidence.  

**Conclusion:**  
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- If the **evidence contains no information** about the claim's subject, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence contains information** that directly supports the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence contains contradictory or conflicting information**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence is incomplete or insufficient**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Output Format:
Provide a clear verdict: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, and a brief reasoning explaining why.

Iteration 27: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a player's name, a team's name, a scientific genus, a song title, etc.), and each value represents a numerical or categorical value associated with that key.

### Task Description

- **Step-by-step Analysis**:  
  - For each key in the evidence, interpret the value and understand what it represents.  
  - Cross-reference the evidence with the claim to determine if the claim is logically supported by the evidence.  
  - Identify any contradictions or missing information that could weaken the claim.  

- **Key Considerations**:  
  - If the claim is about a **specific person, team, event, or object** (e.g., a musician, a song, a player, a scientific genus), then the evidence must directly or indirectly support that claim.  
  - If the claim is about a **general fact** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii has more species than Lantana"), then the evidence must provide numerical or categorical support for that general statement.  
  - If the claim is about a **historical or chronological information** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii was introduced to Hawaii in 1902"), then the evidence must include that specific information or a direct reference to it.  
  - If the claim is about **causality, association, or timing** (e.g., "Silibinin was discovered in 1925"), then the evidence must include that specific time or discovery information.  

- **Final Decision**:  
  - If the claim is **fully supported** by the evidence (i.e., all parts of the claim are directly or indirectly confirmed by the evidence), then the verdict is **SUPPORTED**.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the evidence**: The values may indicate:
   - A presence or absence of a specific attribute (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent).
   - A numerical ranking or category (e.g., 2 = plant, 0 = not a plant).
   - A placeholder or missing data (e.g., 0 = unknown or not recorded).

2. **Analyze the claim**: The claim is a statement about the relationship between two or more entities (e.g., "Arthur Hiller Penn was born before George Kuchar").

3. **Use logical reasoning**: 
   - If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., "George Kuchar was born in 1945" and "Arthur Penn was born in 1940"), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
   - If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

4. **Be careful with ambiguous or incomplete data**: 
   - If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous (e.g., "value: 0" without context), it should not be used to support or refute the claim.
   - If the evidence does not provide any relevant information about the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

5. **Use specific knowledge about the domain**: 
   - The assistant must **not** assume any external knowledge or context beyond the provided evidence.
   - The assistant must **only** use the given evidence to make a judgment.
   - The assistant must **clearly state** the verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) in the final answer.

- The assistant must **only** use the given evidence to make a judgment.
- The assistant must **clearly state** the verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) in the final answer.

- **Ambiguous or incomplete values** (e.g., "value: 0" without context) must be treated as **not recorded** or **unknown**.

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. ### Task Overview:
- The claim is a statement about a specific event, person, or relationship.
- The evidence is a collection of key-value pairs that may provide indirect or direct support for the claim.
- You must analyze the evidence step by step, using logical reasoning and inference to determine if the claim is **supported** or **not supported**.

### Key Considerations:
- **Direct Evidence**: If the claim is directly supported by the evidence (e.g., a specific person is mentioned with a value that matches the claim), then the claim is **supported**.
- **Indirect Evidence**: If the evidence indirectly supports the claim (e.g., a person is associated with a known entity, or a value indicates a connection), then the claim is **supported**.
- **Contradiction or Lack of Evidence**: If the claim is contradicted by the evidence or if no evidence supports it, the claim is **not supported**.

### Example:
**Claim:** "The musician from another band who released a famous album joined the group Zwan shortly after its breakup. *FOL (song)* appeared on this album."

**Evidence:**
- `{'key': 'Zeitgeist (The Smashing Pumpkins album)', 'value': 0}`
- `{'key': 'Zeitgeist (The Smashing Pumpkins album)', 'value': 2}`
- `{'key': 'Jimmy Chamberlin', 'value': 1}`
- `{'key': 'Jimmy Chamberlin', 'value': 2}`
- `{'key': 'FOL (song)', 'value': 0}`

**Reasoning:**
- The album *Zeitgeist* is associated with The Smashing Pumpkins.
- Jimmy Chamberlin is linked to the album, but there is no evidence that he joined Zwan.
- The song *FOL* is associated with the album, but there is no evidence that it appeared on an album from Zwan.

**Conclusion:** The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Analyze each part of the claim and check if it is directly or indirectly supported by the evidence.
- Use the values in the evidence to infer relationships (e.g., high values may indicate popularity, association, or significance).
- If the claim is contradicted or not supported by the evidence, classify it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Output Format:
Provide a final verdict of either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, along with a brief explanation of your reasoning based on the evidence.

3. **Evaluate the relationship**: Determine whether the evidence directly supports, contradicts, or is irrelevant to the claim.
4. **Reason through the evidence**: Use logical reasoning to assess whether the claim can be substantiated by the evidence provided.
5. **Provide a verdict**: Based on your analysis, classify the claim as **SUPPORTED** if the evidence directly supports the claim, or **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the evidence does not support the claim.

### Key Considerations:

- **Relevance**: The evidence must directly relate to the claim. If the evidence is irrelevant, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Multiple entries**: If the same key appears multiple times with different values, this may indicate that the key is associated with multiple entries or that the values are not meaningful (e.g., 0 and 2 may not represent participation or relevance).
- **Specificity**: The claim must be directly supported by the evidence. If the evidence is too general or lacks specificity, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **No evidence**: If the evidence does not provide any information that supports the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

  ```  
Iteration 39: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a player's name, a team's name, a scientific genus, a song title, etc.), and each value represents a numerical or categorical value associated with that key.

### Task Description

- **Step-by-step Analysis**:  
  - For each key in the evidence, interpret the value and understand what it represents.  
  - Cross-reference the evidence with the claim to determine if the claim is logically supported by the evidence.  
  - Identify any contradictions or missing information that could weaken the claim.  

- **Key Considerations**:  
  - If the claim is about a **specific person, team, event, or object** (e.g., a musician, a song, a player, a scientific genus), then the evidence must directly or indirectly support that claim.  
  - If the claim is about a **general fact** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii has more species than Lantana"), then the evidence must provide numerical or categorical support for that general statement.  
  - If the claim is about a **historical or chronological information** (e.g., "Strymon bazochii was introduced to Hawaii in 1902"), then the evidence must include that specific information or a direct reference to it.  
  - If the claim is about **causality, association, or timing** (e.g., "Silibinin was discovered in 1925"), then the evidence must include that specific time or discovery information.  

- **Final Decision**:  
  - If the claim is **fully supported** by the evidence (i.e., all parts of the claim are directly or indirectly confirmed by the evidence), then the verdict is **SUPPORTED**.

   - If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous (e.g., "value: 0" without context), it should not be used to support or refute the claim.
   - If the evidence does not provide any relevant information about the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

5. **Use external knowledge judiciously**: 
   - The assistant must **only** use the given evidence to make a judgment.
   - The assistant must **not** assume any external knowledge or context beyond the provided evidence.
  ```  

  ```  
You are to determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where the keys represent entities (such as events, people, organizations, or locations) and the values represent some form of data (e.g., numerical scores, presence, or relationships). 

### Task Overview:
- **Identify the claim** being evaluated.
- **Analyze the evidence** to determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Use logical reasoning** to assess whether the claim can be substantiated based on the information provided.

### Key Considerations:
- **Entities and relationships**: Identify the entities mentioned in the claim and check if they are present in the evidence.
- **Numerical values**: If values are provided (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 6), interpret them as indicators of relevance, presence, or relationship.
- **Missing information**: If the evidence is incomplete or does not directly address the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the key-value pairs to match entities in the claim to the evidence.
- If the claim is about a specific event, person, or organization, check if the evidence contains relevant data.
- If the claim is about relationships (e.g., ownership, sponsorship, birthplace), use the values to determine if such relationships are supported.
- If the claim cannot be verified or contradicted based on the evidence, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Notes:
- **Entity types**: Recognize entities like people, organizations, events, locations, and roles.
- **Value interpretation**: Understand that values like 0, 1, 2, or 6 are used as indicators (e.g., presence, relevance, or relationship), not as numerical scores.
- **Ambiguity in relationships**: If a relationship is not explicitly stated or is unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Time and context**: If the claim refers to a specific time or event, ensure the evidence includes relevant temporal or contextual data.
- **Role and appearance**: If the claim refers to a specific role or appearance (e.g., "fairy" in a show), the evidence must explicitly mention it.

### Example:
**Claim**: "Swoosie Kurtz was on the episode 15 of the third season of 'Chuck' as a fairy."

**Evidence**:

- The claim refers to Swoosie Kurtz's role in a specific episode of a show.
- The evidence shows she is associated with the show "Chuck" (via "Chuck Versus the Role Models" with value 1), but does not provide any information about her role in the episode or her appearance as a "fairy."
- The value 1 is ambiguous and does not indicate a specific episode or role.

**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

Iteration 53: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents an entity (e.g., a person, company, event, or location) and the value represents some score or indicator (e.g., 0 or 1). You must analyze the evidence step by step to assess the validity of the claim.

### Key Considerations:
- **Entities and their values**: The keys represent entities, and the values represent some form of score or indicator. For example, a value of 1 might indicate a presence, sponsorship, or association, while a value of 0 might indicate absence or no direct link.
- **Claim structure**: The claim is a statement that may involve multiple parts (e.g., "A mid-fifties French golf event on the PGA Tour was sponsored by the company that purchased Mill Street Brewery. It's the largest brewer in the birthplace country of businessman and politician John Sharples, Jr."). You must evaluate each part of the claim against the evidence.
- **Logical connections**: You must determine whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts each part of the claim. If the evidence is insufficient or inconsistent, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **No prior knowledge**: You must rely solely on the provided evidence and the logical connections between the entities and their values to make a verdict.

### Example:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Labatt Open', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Labatt Open', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Labatt Brewing Company', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Mill Street Brewery', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'John Sharples, Jr.', 'value': 0}  

Claim:  
"A mid-fifties French golf event on the PGA Tour was sponsored by the company that purchased Mill Street Brewery. It's the largest brewer in the birthplace country of businessman and politician John Sharples, Jr."

### Task Description:
You are to determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. Reason through the evidence step by step, checking whether the claim's assertions are logically supported by the evidence. If the evidence is insufficient, inconsistent, or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**. If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Identify the claim's components**: Break the claim into individual assertions.
- **Check for direct evidence**: Does the evidence directly support or contradict any part of the claim?
- **Analyze logical relationships**: Are there any implied relationships (e.g., ownership, sponsorship, location) that the evidence supports?
- **Use values as indicators**: Use the values (0 or 1) to determine if an entity is associated with the claim's assertions.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider:
- **Entity values**:
  - A value of **1** typically indicates **presence**, **association**, or **sponsorship**.
  - A value of **0** typically indicates **absence**, **no direct link**, or **non-association**.
- **Claim types**:
  - Claims involving **events**, **organizations**, **people**, **locations**, and **spatial relationships** (e.g., "in the birthplace country of X") need to be evaluated separately.
- **Logical dependencies**:
  - If an entity is mentioned in a claim and has a value of **0**, it is **not** associated with the claim's assertion.
  - If an entity is not mentioned in the claim but has a value of **1**, it may **not** be relevant to the claim unless it is a **supporting entity**.
- **Geographic and cultural context**:
  - Claims involving **birthplace countries**, **regions**, or **cultural groups** (e.g., "Calabrian 'Ndrangheta criminal confederation") must be evaluated against the evidence for **direct association**.

### Final Output:
Provide a clear verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) and a brief explanation of your reasoning based on the evidence.

Iteration 54: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where the keys represent entities (such as events, people, organizations, or locations) and the values represent some form of data (e.g., numerical scores, presence, or relationships). 

### Task Overview:
- **Identify the claim** being evaluated.
- **Analyze the evidence** to determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Use logical reasoning** to assess whether the claim can be substantiated based on the provided information.

### Key Considerations:
- **Entities and relationships**: Identify the entities mentioned in the claim and check if they are present in the evidence.
- **Numerical values**: If values are provided (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 6), interpret them as indicators of relevance, presence, or relationship.
- **Missing information**: If the evidence is incomplete or does not directly address the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
**Claim**: "A mid-fifties French golf event on the PGA Tour was sponsored by the company that purchased Mill Street Brewery. It's the largest brewer in the birthplace country of businessman and politician John Sharples, Jr."

**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'Labatt Open', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Labatt Open', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Labatt Brewing Company', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Mill Street Brewery', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'John Sharples, Jr.', 'value': 0}

**Reasoning**:  
- The claim refers to a specific golf event and a company that purchased a brewery.  
- The evidence does not provide information about the event or the company's ownership of Mill Street Brewery.  
- The value of 2 for Mill Street Brewery is not sufficient to confirm ownership or sponsorship.  
- There is no evidence about the birthplace country of John Sharples, Jr. or his business relationships.  

**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the key-value pairs to match entities in the claim to the evidence.
- If the claim is about a specific event, person, or organization, check if the evidence contains relevant data.
- If the claim is about relationships (e.g., ownership, sponsorship, birthplace), use the values to determine if such relationships are supported.
- If the claim cannot be verified or contradicted based on the evidence, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Additional Notes:
- **Entities and relationships**: Ensure that all entities in the claim are explicitly mentioned in the evidence. If an entity is not present, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Numerical values**: Values like 0, 1, 2, or 6 are interpreted as follows:
  - 0: Not present or not relevant.
  - 1: Present but not strongly indicative of a relationship.
  - 2: Strongly indicative of a relationship or presence.
  - 6: High relevance or strong evidence.
- **Ambiguity and missing information**: If the evidence is unclear, ambiguous, or incomplete, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Logical consistency**: Ensure that the claim and evidence are logically consistent. If the evidence contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer Format:
Provide the final verdict as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, and briefly explain your reasoning.

Iteration 55: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a subject (e.g., a person, a place, a concept, or a phenomenon), and each value represents a numerical score (typically between 0 and 10, with 0 indicating no evidence and 10 indicating strong evidence).

### Task Description

- **Step 1:** Analyze the evidence to understand what each key represents and what the value indicates.  
- **Step 2:** Identify the claim being evaluated and determine whether it is supported by the evidence.  
- **Step 3:** Use logical reasoning to assess whether the claim is consistent with the evidence, taking into account any ambiguity or lack of direct evidence.  
- **Step 4:** Provide a clear and concise verdict: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, and a brief explanation of your reasoning.

### Key Considerations

- **Numerical Values:** A value of 0 typically indicates no direct evidence, while a value of 10 indicates strong evidence.  
- **Ambiguity:** If the evidence does not explicitly state a relationship, the claim may not be fully supported.  
- **General Knowledge:** If the claim involves well-known facts (e.g., historical figures, scientific concepts), use general knowledge to assess support.  
- **Logical Consistency:** Ensure that the claim is logically consistent with the evidence, even if the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous.

### Example

**Inputs**  
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Will Durant', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Margaret Mitchell', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Minoan civilization', 'value': 3}  

Claim: The historian that described the Minoan civilization, and Margaret Mitchell were both philosophical writers.

**Output**  
**Answer: NOT_SUPPORTED**  
**Reasoning:**  
- Will Durant is a historian, not a philosopher, and the evidence does not support him being a philosophical writer.  
- Margaret Mitchell is a novelist, not a philosopher, and the evidence does not support her being a philosophical writer.  
- The Minoan civilization has a value of 3, indicating it is associated with a writer or philosopher, but this is not explicitly stated.  

### Feedback Guidelines

- If the verdict is **SUPPORTED**, the assistant must clearly explain why the claim is supported by the evidence.  
- If the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, the assistant must clearly explain why the claim is not supported, even if the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous.

### Final Answer Format

```  
**Answer:** SUPPORTED/NOT_SUPPORTED  
**Reasoning:** [brief explanation of your reasoning]  
```  
```  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information

- **Numerical scoring:** The values in the evidence are assumed to represent a scale (e.g., 0 = no evidence, 10 = strong evidence).  
- **Ambiguity in evidence:** If the evidence does not directly support the claim, the claim may still be considered **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- **General knowledge:** If the claim involves well-known facts (e.g., historical figures, scientific concepts), the assistant should use general knowledge to assess support.  
- **Logical consistency:** The claim must be logically consistent with the evidence, even if the evidence is incomplete.  
- **No direct evidence:** If the evidence does not directly support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

You are to determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where the keys represent entities (such as events, people, organizations, or locations) and the values represent some form of data (e.g., numerical scores, presence, or relationships). 

### Task Overview:
- **Identify the claim** being evaluated.
- **Analyze the evidence** to determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Use logical reasoning** to assess whether the claim can be substantiated based on the information provided.

### Key Considerations:
- **Entities and relationships**: Identify the entities mentioned in the claim and check if they are present in the evidence.
- **Numerical values**: If values are provided (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 6), interpret them as indicators of relevance, presence, or relationship.
- **Missing information**: If the evidence is incomplete or does not directly address the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the key-value pairs to match entities in the claim to the evidence.
- If the claim is about a specific event, person, or organization, check if the evidence contains relevant data.
- If the claim is about relationships (e.g., ownership, sponsorship, birthplace), use the values to determine if such relationships are supported.
- If the claim cannot be verified or contradicted based on the evidence, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Notes:
- **Entity types**: Recognize entities like people, organizations, events, locations, and roles.
- **Value interpretation**: Understand that values like 0, 1, 2, or 6 are used as indicators (e.g., presence, relevance, or relationship), not as numerical scores.
- **Ambiguity in relationships**: If a relationship is not explicitly stated or is unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Time and context**: If the claim refers to a specific time or event, ensure the evidence includes relevant temporal or contextual data.
- **Role and appearance**: If the claim refers to a specific role or appearance (e.g., "fairy" in a show), the evidence must explicitly mention it.

### Example:
**Claim**: "Swoosie Kurtz was on the episode 15 of the third season of 'Chuck' as a fairy."

**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'Chuck Versus the Role Models', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Swoosie Kurtz', 'value': 1}

   - If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous (e.g., "value: 0" without context), it should not be used to support or refute the claim.
   - If the evidence does not provide any relevant information about the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- The assistant must **not** assume any external knowledge or context beyond the provided evidence.
- The assistant must **only** use the given evidence to make a judgment.
- The assistant must **clearly state** the verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) in the final answer.

Iteration 61: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**, which is a collection of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific entity (e.g., person, book, magazine, plant, etc.), and each value represents a numerical indicator (e.g., 0, 1, 2, etc.) that may indicate a specific attribute or status of the entity.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the evidence**: The values may indicate:
   - A presence or absence of a specific attribute (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent).
   - A numerical ranking or category (e.g., 2 = plant, 0 = not a plant).
   - A placeholder or missing data (e.g., 0 = unknown or not recorded).

2. **Analyze the claim**: The claim is a statement about the relationship between two or more entities (e.g., "Arthur Hiller Penn was born before George Kuchar").

3. **Use logical reasoning**:
   - If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., "George Kuchar was born in 1945" and "Arthur Penn was born in 1940"), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
   - If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

4. **Be careful with ambiguous or incomplete data**:
   - If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous (e.g., "value: 0" without context), it should not be used to support or refute the claim.
   - If the evidence does not provide any relevant information about the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Important Notes:
- The assistant must **not** assume any external knowledge or context beyond the provided evidence.
- The assistant must **only** use the given evidence to make a judgment.
- The assistant must **clearly state** the verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) in the final answer.

### Example:
- **Input**:  
  ```  
  Evidence:  
  {'key': 'George Kuchar', 'value': 0}  
  {'key': 'Arthur Penn', 'value': 0}  
  Claim: Arthur Hiller Penn was born before George Kuchar.  
  ```  
  **Output**: **NOT_SUPPORTED**  
  *Reasoning*: The evidence does not provide any information about the birth dates of George Kuchar or Arthur Penn. Therefore, the claim cannot be supported.

- **Input**:  
  ```  
  Evidence:  
  {'key': 'Dionne Bunsha', 'value': 1}  
  {'key': 'Frontline (magazine)', 'value': 0}  
  {'key': 'Scarred: Experiments with Violence in Gujarat', 'value': 1}  
  Claim: The author of *Scarred: Experiments with Violence in Gujarat* worked for the magazine published by The Hindu Group.  
  ```  
  **Output**: **NOT_SUPPORTED**  
  *Reasoning*: The evidence shows that Dionne Bunsha is associated with the book *Scarred: Experiments with Violence in Gujarat* (value: 1), but it does not indicate that she worked for the magazine published by The Hindu Group (value: 0). Therefore, the claim cannot be supported based on the given evidence.

### Additional Notes:
- **Entity Identification**: The keys represent entities (e.g., "George Kuchar", "Arthur Penn", "Scarred: Experiments with Violence in Gujarat"), and the values represent attributes or statuses of these entities.
- **Attribute Interpretation**: The values may indicate:
  - A presence or absence of a specific attribute (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent).
  - A numerical ranking or category (e.g., 2 = plant, 0 = not a plant).
  - A placeholder or missing data (e.g., 0 = unknown or not recorded).
- **Logical Deduction**: The assistant must use only the provided evidence and not make assumptions or use external knowledge.
- **Ambiguity Handling**: If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous, the assistant must conclude **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Claim Analysis**: The claim is about the **relationship** between two or more entities, and the assistant must determine if the evidence supports, contradicts, or is irrelevant to that relationship.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Check for direct support**: If the evidence directly provides the necessary information to confirm or deny the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Check for contradiction**: If the evidence contradicts the claim or lacks necessary information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Use logical inference**: If the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer:
**SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, depending on the evidence and reasoning.

Iteration 62: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where the keys represent entities (such as events, people, organizations, or locations) and the values represent some form of data (e.g., numerical scores, presence, or relationships). 

### Task Overview:
- **Identify the claim** being evaluated.
- **Analyze the evidence** to determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Use logical reasoning** to assess whether the claim can be substantiated based on the information provided.

### Key Considerations:
- **Entities and relationships**: Identify the entities mentioned in the claim and check if they are present in the evidence.
- **Numerical values**: If values are provided (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 6), interpret them as indicators of relevance, presence, or relationship.
- **Missing information**: If the evidence is incomplete or does not directly address the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the key-value pairs to match entities in the claim to the evidence.
- If the claim is about a specific event, person, or organization, check if the evidence contains relevant data.
- If the claim is about relationships (e.g., ownership, sponsorship, birthplace), use the values to determine if such relationships are supported.
- If the claim cannot be verified or contradicted based on the evidence, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Notes:
- **Entity types**: Recognize entities like people, organizations, events, locations, and roles.
- **Value interpretation**: Understand that values like 0, 1, 2, or 6 are used as indicators (e.g., presence, relevance, or relationship), not as numerical scores.
- **Ambiguity in relationships**: If a relationship is not explicitly stated or is unclear, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Time and context**: If the claim refers to a specific time or event, ensure the evidence includes relevant temporal or contextual data.
- **Role and appearance**: If the claim refers to a specific role or appearance (e.g., "fairy" in a show), the evidence must explicitly mention it.
- **Entity uniqueness**: Ensure that the entities in the claim are uniquely identified in the evidence, or that the evidence provides sufficient context to infer the claim.

### Example:
**Claim**: "Swoosie Kurtz was on the episode 15 of the third season of 'Chuck' as a fairy."

**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'Chuck Versus the Role Models', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Swoosie Kurtz', 'value': 1}  

**Reasoning**:  
- The claim refers to Swoosie Kurtz's role in a specific episode of a show.
- The evidence shows she is associated with the show "Chuck" (via "Chuck Versus the Role Models" with value 1), but does not provide any information about her role in the episode or her appearance as a "fairy."
- The value 1 is ambiguous and does not indicate a specific episode or role.

**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Answer Format:
Provide the final verdict as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, and briefly explain your reasoning.
